date: 2015-12-19
to: Alex Shevelenko <alex@glocalpartners.com>
subject: Re: Fwd: thank you for shaping relayto in 2015, Amy...
msg_id: 151bacaaeab5ca4b
---

I've been hearing a lot about personalised subject lines seeing lower open
rates because of over personalisation. Maybe worth a/b testing, as it might
resonate better in a marketing/sales/business demographic.

I would combine the two awards bullets

I don't think it's absolutely necessary for this email as its more of a
seasonal update, but we should begin to think about where outside of
reading the emails the audience should be driven to engage. I could see it
being twitter, linkedin, obviously on platform, spurring users on to
recruit other users via email, etc. Each has pros and cons, but generally
you want to be driving a follow action from a campaign like this (follow us
on linkedin to stay up to date / refer your friends for access to beta
features, etc.).

benefits listed below, and we're certainly open to suggestions). I'd be
happy to answer any higher level questions you may have about
Startupbootcamp and our programs. I've also cc'ed Nick and Megan who are
running our events in the USA and can provide any details on the Atlanta
event and coordinate logistics.

date: 2015-12-16
to: Christine Eisner <ce3136@gmail.com>
subject: Startupbootcamp Event in Atlanta during aTVFest
msg_id: 151abb6cde20b489
---

Event Page:
http://www.startupbootcamp.org/events/sbc-fintech-nyc-atlanta-fasttrack.html

We'd be very interested to run this under aTVFest or as an independent
event at a SCAD venue in early Feb 2016 (tentatively 4th of Feb). We've
talked to ATV, and it doesn't seem like a great fit.

The NYC program is specifically oriented around FinTech, but as FinTech is
the foundation for any sort of e-commerce and digital payments, thought it
might fit in very well to the rest of the program. Also, Jesse Podell, the
MD of the program, was the former founder of Tech Day (a significant Tech
Event in NYC and a few other locations now), as well as a serial
entrepreneur in the digital finance industry.

*Benefits to Host:*
-Priority application for alumni/students/staff to apply to pitch for
potential investment
-Potential to open the event to students or public to get insight on
building companies and the startup ecosystem
-Branding/cross-promotion through Startupbootcamp channels (50k+ web visits
per month, 100k+ social followers) and general alignment with technology
innovation ecosystem
-Potential to provide a mentor to the panel
-Potential cobranded push of main/sub-events for aTVFest
-Potentially providing Jesse or one of our mentors to do a fireside chat or
keynote for attendees or students



See below our general outreach emails:

Hi [VENUE] team,

This is Nick from the StartupBootcamp Fintech team. I am getting in touch
as I would like to find out whether you would be interested and available
to work with us in hosting a Startup 'FastTrack' day event in Atlanta which
are planning to have on Feb 4. As a bit of background, StartupBootcamp is a
global family of startup accelerators with a collaborative and mentor
focused approach aimed at encouraging innovation.

As part of our just launched SBC Fintech NYC program
<http://t.sidekickopen35.com/e1t/c/5/f18dQhb0S7lC8dDMPbW2n0x6l2B9nMJN7t5XZsQsBhjW1qMyFK5wvHZnVRJgRK56dP4Wf34C7ZF02?t=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.startupbootcamp.org%2Faccelerator%2Ffintech-new-york.html&si=5804247449337856&pi=287af81f-8d00-4210-f158-a853ea6ee9ad>,
we are now looking for the best and most enthusiastic Fintech startups
across America and globally to join our 2016 cohort. FastTracks are pitch
days where we invite up to 10 startups to pitch and provide them with
feedback and 1-on-1 mentoring. This is free for the applicants with no
further obligations to our program. We look at FastTracks as a way to
connect with ambitious Fintech startups for our program, as well as a great
way to promote and connect the local Fintech startup ecosystem and bring
interest to the venues which host us.

We ideally need the below for the event, so do let me know if this could
work in your space:
- a larger room that can host 20-25 people seated
- projector and large screen for pitches
- 5 tables with 4-5 chairs for the feedback sessions
- a small break out area for lunch and networking
- no registration necessary

We would be delighted if you would consider being our hosting venue and
very much look forward in hearing from you,

Nick

subject: Re: Sponsorship Material

---

One thing I've also found that also often can work for these is listing a
limited number of the more premium sponsorships - creates a bit of urgency
in terms of signing partners, and you can always add some additional
one-off services if there's demand beyond what we anticipate.

I also think maybe listing a mention in a post-event recap email blast

subject: Re: Eureka Park
msg_id: 15168502eaee3097
---

Hi Sasha,

As we are not ourselves a startup, we probably wouldn't be looking for
exhibition space. We're an investment company with a portfolio of 300
startups. Our involvement at events is generally more along the lines of
running pitch competitions, serving as judges/keynotes/panel speakers, or
curating panels in collaboration with our corporate partners (our panels at
Slush and Web Summit all sold out).

We will be running recruitment events for potential investment companies
while we're in Las Vegas, so offering a streamlined path for investment as
a result of their participation at Eureka Park could be a great way to add
value for your customers (I know we were a bit frustrated at Incident
Technologies after our experience at CES in terms of the return on
investment we felt it provided). There are a number of ways I could see a
mutually beneficial cross promotion around this taking form.

If Eureka Park only provides exhibition space and doesn't actually do any
programming, I don't think it would really be of interest to us. However,
if you're open to a more significant involvement from a startup
accelerator/investment firm, we'd love to participate.

Best,

Matthew

date: 2015-11-10
to: Christine Eisner <ce3136@gmail.com>
subject: photo instructions for sarah
msg_id: 150ef01fd0a1e1b2
---

STEP 1:
-Crop and resize the 3 images below to 1400x470 pixels
*- Photo 1: **https://drive.google.com/open?id=0B-zvWZ1FktiFU3BIenVkZ2NCTHM
<https://drive.google.com/open?id=0B-zvWZ1FktiFU3BIenVkZ2NCTHM>*
- *Photo 2:* *https://drive.google.com/open?id=0B-zvWZ1FktiFQ1NGNDQtNG1mdlk
<https://drive.google.com/open?id=0B-zvWZ1FktiFQ1NGNDQtNG1mdlk>*
- *Photo 3:** https://drive.google.com/open?id=0B-zvWZ1FktiFOENNZm4tVHEyeDg
<https://drive.google.com/open?id=0B-zvWZ1FktiFOENNZm4tVHEyeDg>*

STEP 2:
-Go to "appearance" in the menu on the left hand side of wordpress, then go
to "customize"

STEP 3:
-Go to "theme options", then go to "theme slider options"

STEP 4: click "change image", then click the "upload files" tab in the
upper left hand corner

STEP 5: find the images you want on your computer to upload. the tab will
automatically switch back to the "media library" with the image you
uploaded last selected. click "choose image". it may take a second to reload

STEP 6: repeat step 4 and 5 the same for the other two images (scroll down
in the left customization menu to find them)

Berkeley, UCSD, Stanford, UChicago, Columbia, Cornell, maybe Michigan. I do
really miss consumer behavior research, although at least I still get to
dabble and hone some skills with bigger datasets.

I've actually never worked with Ivan at all! Social Coin is one of 300
companies Startupbootcamp has accelerated/invested in - I only happened to
connect with him when he responded to an email I sent to all 300 of them
about free tickets I had to give away to a conference. But those 300
startups highlights one of the reasons I'm okay not doing a PhD yet - I
have access to one of the deepest datasets on startups here, and it's my
job to clean it, optimize collection, and generate insight from it with the
help of a few python developers.

I'd be more happy to tell you more, and would love your input on my PhD
process - I'm sure the landscape has changed quite a bit since I last
really took the time to do thorough research on who's researching what
where. Also, my company is launching our second program in the US in NYC
next week (we launched Miami this week - usually we space them out a bit
more :D ), which actually could be something interesting for you to get
involved in.

If you want to hop on a skype and catch up a bit in the next week or so,
I'd really love to hear what you've been working on as of late - frankly I
find your work much more interesting than mine! Would there be a time in
the next week or two that might work for you? Remind me to tell you about
medical behavioral research standards :)

Hope all is well!

Matthew

date: 2015-10-28
to: Gregory Goltsov <gregory@goltsov.info>
subject: Website Proposal
msg_id: 150ae92c45aea9f5
---

What do you think of this? Going to send it to our directorWhy switch CMS?

MODx Evolution is outdated.

During the last year I’ve run into numerous bugs, structural disasters,
bloated code, errors, and generally a very unstable site.

In the future Startupbootcamp is only going to grow. More accelerators
means more content on the website, more staff accessing the site on a daily
basis, and more users visiting.
The biggest errors, bugs, and restrictions:

   1.

   Timeouts (error 500), site doesn’t respond. Database is messy and slow.
   2.

   Generally very unstable.
   3.

   Pages in MODx not showing when published.
   4.

   Backend scripts breaking randomly.
   5.

   Slow control panel.
   6.

   Outdated WYSIWYG text editor.
   7.

   No customizable permission setup in control panel.
   8.

   No SEO integration.
   9.

   No responsive/mobile optimization.
   10.

   No version control/ difference in dev and production setup.
   1.

      Not having a staging server potentially breaks the live site when
      developing.



Every week, at least 10 hours of work goes to bugfixing and error handling
instead of improving and optimising - just from my side (Alexander). On top
of this comes the confusion and frustration from the programs, specifically
the MMs and people responsible for updating sponsors, mentors and alumni.

Listed below are three different options for moving forward and improving
the website.

Any one of these options includes switching to AWS or Google Cloud.


1. Sticking to MODx - moving to Revolution

We’re currently running MODx Evo (Evolution) v. 1.0.3 which is outdated,
unstable, and bloated. The community around Evo is as good as dead thus so
is the support and development of plugins.

One option going forward is to update/switch to MODx Revo (Revolution)
which is their newer version.
Pros:

   -

   Still supported by community.
   -

   Updated regularly.
   -

   Switching is relatively fast since the systems are alike.
   -

   Frontend doesn’t need recode. A lot of copy/pasting can be done.
   -

   The cheapest option.

Cons:

   -

   All scripts needs to be rewritten to Revo syntax.
   -

   Control Panel UX doesn’t improve a lot.
   -

   Easy to move everything over without cleaning up.
   -

   Time consuming when it’s only a temporary solution.
   -

   Most PHP CMS are vulnerable.
   -

   We’re a tech company. We should keep up with the new tech.
   -

   No version control (Github etc.) + no staging environment.
   -

   Apache (necessary for running PHP) servers doesn’t scale in the cloud.



This is the cheapest option of the three.


2. Moving (back) to Wordpress

Before SBC switched to MODx, the website was running Wordpress. This was
before my time so I don’t know why the decision to move away from Wordpress
was made. From log files it looks like the switch was done back in 2012.
Pros:

   -

   Great community support.
   -

   Fast and updated development.
   -

   Great and simple UI/UX.
   -

   Huge database of plugins available.
   -

   Easy to customize control panel to fit our needs.
   -

   Fast setup.
   -

   Relatively easy to build templates by copy/pasting the design from
   current site.
   -

   Most commonly used CMS (Matthew and likely a few MMs have used this
   extensively before)

Cons:

   -

   Build for small/medium sites with main focus on blogs.
   -

   Might not be able to handle the amount of heavy content.
   -

   We’re a tech company. We should keep up with the new tech.
   -

   No version control (Github etc.) + no staging environment.
   -

   Most PHP CMS are vulnerable.
   -

   WP plugins are famous for being security risks.
   -

   Apache (necessary for running PHP) servers doesn’t scale in the cloud.




Medium priced option.

3. Moving to another CMS (Wagtail etc.)

After talking to a bunch of different devs, it stands out pretty clearly
that PHP based CMS are outdated and a general security risk. Most of them
refer to something Django/Python based like Wagtail CMS (https://wagtail.io).


Django is a new and upcoming framework for the language called Python. Both
Django and Python have thriving communities all around the world.

Wagtail is an open source CMS built on Django. Example of use:
https://torchbox.com/work/royal-college-art/
Pros:

   -

   Completely new architecture.
   -

   Version control + staging environment.
   -

   Django is relatively easy to learn.
   -

   Built to scale, both architecture and cloud hosting.
   -

   Minimal security risk.
   -

   Clean up of deprecated content.
   -

   New control panel built for us.
   -

   Stable system.
   -

   Great UX/UI in control panel.
   -

   Fully customizable.
   -

   Long term solution.
   -

   Can handle large sites and large amounts of content.

Cons:

   -

   No in-house experienced Django devs.
   -

   All content needs to be moved.
   -

   Most expensive solution.
   -

   Most time consuming solution.
   -

   All scripts and custom functionality needs to be rewritten.

to: Nikita Korotaev <nikita@glocalpartners.com>
subject: Relayto Questions
msg_id: 150a966739a96c5c
---

Hi Nikita,

We;re onboarding on to Relayto at Startupbootcamp, and our producer had a
few questions:

1) Is there a way to align or center the heading text on slides?
2) is there a way to set a background for a slide as opposed to inserting
an image inline (i.e. we have some very wide images and would prefer to
show a larger image with overlaid text than frame the image with text). If
not, can we set a presentation background? It seems the advanced settings

date: 2015-10-20
to: Matt Thomas <matt@brawlforacause.com>
subject: Re: Followup and Brawl for a Cause
msg_id: 1508709e8fad29fa
---

Hey man,

Hope all is well! Sorry for the delay, but I finally got a few minutes to
crack through your site. I must say, it looks good aesthetically. I do have
a few tips.

Also, before I dive in, few hiring plugs in case you might be looking at
Roadie or know anyone who is - more than happy to make an intro:
-Former Sony Mobile VP of Marketing who relocated to Atlanta for his wife
and is looking to get into startups - frankly would be a killer head of
marketing or biz dev hire
-A friend from Paideia who has been running AdWords and works events for a
travel company. He graduated UGA a year before you. Looking for an entry
Biz Dev role at a startup.


On to your site:

1. The gif background might be destroying your page load time (it depends
on how it's structured). Check what your load time looks like in Google
Webmastertools - if it's above 2 seconds, then the gif is uncompressed
and/or loads simultaneously with the page instead of after. Also, because
the gif can take a bit to load, it takes a while to get to actual images of
boxing - I would redo the gif so that if someones on a shitty connection,
they see boxing instead of you/the crowd

2. Calls to action: the best advice i can give you here is map out the
different user journies of the inbound you would want (fighters, press,
partners, volunteers, donators?) and what the ideal proportion of each
would be. There's no solid rule for how many CTA's to have, but I see your
home page as having a big button for fighter sign up, and then maybe 2 more
smaller ones for partner and donations directly under it. I would then
break out the hamburger menu, combine it with the bottom menu, and put it
at the top. Or maybe you're better off having just a fighter sign up and a
contact us button or email form submission. Optimizely is very solid for
easy CTA, copy, and simple aesthetic A/B testing - maybe worth doing that -
but make sure you wait for statistical significance, which could take a few
months.

3. Hamburger menu: it does make it easier to have a mobile site, but i
would avoid on desktop, and even mobile if possible.

4. Is your site built on wordpress? If so, create me a temporary account so
I can dig through your SEO. If you give me edit access and have Yoast SEO
installed, I can even implement changes if you want. It looks like there's
some major arbitrage there from Googling around.

5. Mobile: streamline it - have a solid description and a strong call to
action (probably either email or fighter sign up) and a button to continue
to the full website - all visible without scrolling. mobile is huge for SEO
now. it's also a massive headache.

6. Content: as much as you can do to flesh out your content around topics
related to boxing, charities, the cities you're in, your fighters, etc. the
better.

7. Press: this is huge - a big inbound link could really be huge for you to
break into search rankings - start small - write up a semi-generic press
release for an event you can easily reuse, make a list of publication
contacts, and focus on getting niche blog posts at first. Once you have 10
or so, gather up all the links and send them to larger local outlets. keep
building the pyramid up like that. bonus points

8. Social: get socialbro for a month and compile databases. search for
everyone with boxer or boxing in their name in a specific area who has
tweeted recently - you'll have more leads for potential fighters than
you'll know what to do with. then, before an event, get a month
subscription to buffer awesome, write 10 cold outreach tweets with room to
put a handle at the beginning (the @ tag makes it not show up on your
profile for desktop users), then copy it around in a spreadsheet, save it
as text, remove the commas, upload it into bulk buffer which will port it
in to buffer. you can cold tweet at 100 people per day with 10 minutes of
work this way (and more on less time if you shell out for bigger
subscriptions). I can do a screencapture video of this if the formatting of
the spreadsheet is confusing.

I've also linked a landing page analysis I did for Touch Surgery, just so
you can see what I was saying with mobile landing pages.

I know that's a ton, so let me know if you want to hop on a skype or
something to go over it. I tried to make it a balance of quick fixes and
sustainable, potentially scalable efforts.

https://www.dropbox.com/s/fmvtbt95b76vt1c/Landing%20Page%20Best%20Practices.pptx?dl=0

Hope all is well!

Matthew

subject: Re: England Trip, December
msg_id: 150512cdddb624ac
---

Neighbourhoods in London that you might like that arent ridiculously
expensive and very easy to get into London from with good surrounding
coffee shops

Shoreditch
Aldgate
Angel
Southwark
Bethnal Green
Hackney

All of the ones above except southwark are basically in an area of london
that is compared very often with brooklyn. Lots of great coffee shops, pho
shops, markets, etc. Basically looks just east of central London and the
northmost part of the part of London south of the Thames. avoid west London
or south London unless it's right by the Thames. Kings Cross also is a
decent area to look (north - right next to angel).

London is definitely ridiculously expensive, and especially after the
recent tumble in euro value, Berlin is super cheap and probably my 2nd
favourite city in the world.

Other places maybe worth considering (no idea where you've been in Europe):
South of France (Aix, Montpellier, Nice, Toulouse)
Prague
Budapest
Barcelona
Belgium
Vienna

All of those would be much cheaper than london. I also love Switzerland,
but its craaaaazy expensive. And I also recently heard from my friend who
spent the last 18 months traveling the world that Copenhagen is his
favourite city - I've never been

date: 2015-10-09
to: Deirdre Hirschtritt <deirdre.hirschtritt@gmail.com>
subject: Re: England Trip, December
msg_id: 1504da24a9020824
---

Heyyo!

Is the event in Birmingham at the NEC? I had to work an event there earlier
this year - Birmingham is a pretty ridiculously boring place, and as from a
timing standpoint, the UK is pretty much dead during Christmas, as it's
technically a Christian country. Downtown Birmingham is okay though, and an
easy train ride from the NEC. My personal plans for that time period are
probably to be in London or maybe south of France for New Years. I'd be
back by the 2nd though, if I ended up going to France.

Obviously December 31 is a big night in London - so if you could get down
in time (it's a 2 hour train ride from the NEC in Birmingham to Kings Cross
station in London), that might be fun. If I'm there, you're welcome to join
in whatever I'm doing, or there's plennnnnty of other stuff to do around
the UK.

As per getting around the UK, it's very easy - you can take trains almost
anywhere, although if you're going to Scotland or Ireland, you should fly -
it'll be about the same price and half the time (if not less). I would also
say the same to Wales if you're coming from Birmingham, as you'd likely
have to connect through London if you were taking a train. Places in the UK
that I particularly like - Nottingham, Bristol, Edinburgh, and Brighton.
I've never been to Wales or Ireland though. Bristol and Brighton would
probably force you to go through London if you were on a train, although I
would potentially even look into flights for those. Bristol is a great
place to go if you're into arts and Brighton is basically the San Francisco
of the UK. Edinburgh will probably be very cold, and Nottingham isn't
really that great. In general, I would recommend AirBnB for lodging, and
Uber works in quite a few cities (although not all - it's much much cheaper
than cab though). I think Oxford might be bad timing, as all the students
will be gone and as a result much of the town's restaurants and shops may
not be open. Still, it's beautiful there.

You could also go pretty much anywhere in Europe - it might be a little
more expensive than usually due to the holiday season, but if you book now
you could probably find a flight to pretty much anywhere in Europe via
RyanAir, EasyJet, or Wizz. Don't do the EuroStar/Chunnel - it's so
expensive - usually just cheaper (although sometimes slower) to fly to
Paris and hop on a TGV from there if you're going anywhere on the Iberian
Peninsula.

Hope that answers all your questions - let me know if you have any more or
what you decide!

Best,

Matthew

Let me know what you decide on!

date: 2015-10-07
to: Sam Ahmed <sam@startupbootcamp.org>
subject: Initial Data Rundown
msg_id: 150427fe99364e36
---

Goals:

   - Optimise candidate targeting by unearthing factors that correlate to
   post-SBC success
   - Optimise recruitment path (order and frequency of touch points) to
   increase conversions (i.e. accepted offers)
   - Provide data to aid in selection process to reduce false positives and
   negatives
   - Evaluate individual program performance and push feedback to create
   informational social conformity
   - Benchmark overall SBC performance
   - Generally optimise the recruitment funnel (there are likely elements
   outside of the scope of the dataset I was provided)


First steps:

   - Complete collection and cleaning of the data Alex was working on
   - Redesign survey/application forms for better data collection, to
   provide a few more factors we can analyse, and generally complete the scope
   of the data (i.e. post-incubation data)
   - Identify biases in selection process and make programs aware so can
   compensate if undesirable
   - Identify desirable factors of recruits that indicate future success


A more out-there idea:

   - Compare ourselves to other accelerators/incubators - by adding the
   question "Have you applied to other accelerators/incubators" we could gain
   data on other programs' rejections. Scraping public data will give us the
   data on their acceptances. Subsequently using machine learning could give
   us truly unique predictive analytics on the startup ecosystem.


Reports:
5 examples of items I could see in the reports:
-Geographic breakdown of acceptances (there seems to be an extremely heavy
bias towards targeting and accepting local startups, but where else are
hotbeds?)
-Channel targeting breakdown (which channels have highest proportional
acceptance rate, lowest proportional acceptance rate, lead to our
objectively ideal applicant?)
-Trends in teams (it seems that in general, programs like teams with small
number cofounders, lots of employees, but not too many engineers)
-Suggesting that some startups may be better fits in an alternative program
(would need available info on status of recruiting at each program)
-Outline previously missed opportunities and general trends in decision
making (would need subsequent information on startup success)

to: "Jeffrey Martín" <jefdonmar@gmail.com>
subject: Re: Help
msg_id: 1503d70514a42c5d
---

Hey guys,

My feedback:

-the market size slides look weird - first one is cluttered and second has
odd spacing
-competition makes it look like you're going after women oriented
non-profits - i would make your competition programs like code academy,
general assembly, etc.
-on the business plan slide - i would simplify i - it looks like a bunch of
cells are invisible or cut-off - make everything fit on one page. i would
google "revenue projection"or "business model" and see what you get for
inspiration - group revenues and expenses by category, not as line items
(i.e. as vague categories: product design, program launch, employee
expense, program administration, etc; instead of very specific items).
Really you'd be better off consulting with someone finance oriented to find
out exactly what they'd want to see - my intuition is that you might be
projecting conservatively? I'm of the same philosophy in theory, but in
practice you need to shoot for the stars or no one will give you time of
day - again, this is not my focus though
-customer acquisition - make this slide visual (add photos or something)
-images on the team slide are warped - use canva for cropping/image
production so as not to skew aspect ratio - i would also make the text in
the team section a little bit larger
-5 year plan is a great slide, but very text heavy - try to make one-line
bullets and the elaborate as you talk

Very impressed - i would also keep in mind that especially as you're trying
to raise early funding, you're really playing on peoples emotions as
opposed to rationality - considering that, i would try and think as much as
you can about the narrative you'll be telling in the beginning of your
pitch around the problem and how you transition into solution.

When does this need to be completely done by? I can try and dig up some
financial forecasting slides tonight

I just wanted to let you know that I'll be leaving Touch Surgery in a week
or so to take over as the startup recruitment and marketing manager for the
11 branches of Startupbootcamp - that being said, if you ever have friends
working on interesting early stage tech/startups, please tell them to reach
out to me. Also, as we branch out into medical verticals, I'd love to get
you involved as a mentor/advisor to some of the companies working on health
tech solutions, although that's a ways off right now.

Really, I wanted to let you know that you were one of the most enjoyable
people I worked with in my time at Touch Surgery, and only wish we had had
more opportunities to do so. I've mentioned you to my replacements and will
leave them with your email, if that's okay.

Also, I've been following your posts on the NHS recently, and must say,
it's been very useful to see not to mention very articulate. If you're
interested, I'm grabbing coffee with the editor of News-Medical in a week
or so, and could ask her if she'd be open to having you pen a piece on it.

Phase 1: SEO/ASO implementation

strategy plan/action items beyond initial scope
Estimated Time Required: 15 hours

Phase 2: Analytics Customisation/Growth Hacking Plan

tracking and analysis (usage/engagement, seo, aso, and digital mkt),
setting up channel attribution for web and downloads, outlining
documentation and protocol for growth hacking
Estimated Time Required: 10 hours

Phase 3: Extended SEO/ASO implementation
Consists of: a/b testing, conversion optimisation, linkbuilding, directory
listings, SEO implementation across new pages (as outlined in future
strategy plan), grey hat strategies, ASO targeting
Estimated Time Required: 20 hours

date: 2015-09-14
to: Michele Parkins <micheleparkins@gmail.com>
subject: Re: SEO work inquiry
msg_id: 14fccdb664330cfa
---

Hi Michele,

I certainly have a bit of availability to help with what you're working on
- sounds very interesting!

Just for your reference, SEO can be broken down into 3 broad categories -
1) architectural, 2) on-page, and 3) off-page. Architectural refers to how
you have your site structured and tagged for Google, On-page refers to the
actual text and content on the pages, and Off-page refers to link building
(i.e. press, social media pages, directories, etc.). Generally for projects
like this, I'd be most cost-effective working on Architectural and On-page,
as Off-page is a much more time intensive and drawn out process (not to
mention is accomplished by related activities such as PR more effectively
and is compounded by good architecture and on-page SEO).

The first steps are probably to hop on a call for 10 or 15 minutes just so
I can hear a bit more about the customers you are trying to target and how
you see the platform and website expanding in the future to get a better
idea of the work involved. I'll be on the east coast US from Sunday for 2
weeks, so it might be easiest to chat sometime early next week since we'll
be in the same time zone? Or if you're looking to get started right away, I
can do a call pretty much anytime after 8 PM or so UK time Tues/Weds/Thurs
this week.

In the meantime, do you know what content management system you're using
(i.e. wix, wordpress, college publisher, weebly, etc.)? I also noticed that
it seems you've had some issues porting your blog over from your old site -
that's certainly something I could help with if you have the old blog
content - and blogs are a great way to expand SEO.

Thank you for the kind words - and of course my best to you, Kim, and the
kids!

Matthew

date: 2015-09-10
to: Dean <d.eisner@comcast.net>
subject: Re: FYI: Kocomojo Announces New Proximity Marketing Platform
msg_id: 14fb75ba9fca394e
---

Beacons are a thing, but of questionable efficacy up til now (there have
been a few campaigns that have relied on beacons to decent efficacy). I've
actually been speaking to someone who is involved with a beacon based
social network that apparently is taking off very rapidly with primary
school children and skateboarders. There are quite a few platform based
barriers to this, although my personal opinion is that the last social
startup will be location oriented (YikYak and Snapchat are getting there,
but don't provide real value based on location yet), and likely will
involve beacons in some way. THE BIG ISSUE WITH BEACONS IS THAT THERE IS NO
STANDARD YET. It's looking like it will be NFC, as that's what iPhone is
using for Apple Pay, but some mnfctrs still havent bought it. Also, people
who do have it available haven't gotten in to the habit of using NFC
scanning.

GPS triggered marketing is far more immediately interesting to me, as it
ties in very well to mobile, and mobile is flipping the digital marketing
space upside down in a way. It looks like they have some cool integrations
that could be used for in app ad serving that would be pretty useful.

Looks pretty interesting all in all. Happy to chat a bit more when I call
you tonight.

Hi Andy,

Great! Knowing that ideas as aspirational as the documentary were on
target, I have a few others along those lines. I must say, this job is
sounding more and more fun.

-Some sort of award aimed at inventors, think Disrupt for MVPs - winner
gets small funding to get to the point they could apply for acceleration
-Find cofounders or team members meetups including pitch sessions/speed
dating/expert panels (panels create stakeholders). I went to one of these
at Google Campus a few weeks ago, and it was actually quite fun and looked
to be productive. Not to mention it seems there's a strong trend from the
data in favouring 2+ member teams. This would allow us to get info and
market to super early stage startups that might become good candidates for
acceleration, as well as help them become better candidates.
-Investor relations marketing - whitepapers/analyses could provide value to
corporate sponsors, or at least brand us as a thought leader
-Create partnerships with existing startup listing sites sites
(startupstartup, product hunt, angellist, f6s, coworking spaces, etc) or
create our own resource to track early stage startups (likely submission
based). This would allow us to build an advantage in identifying good
candidates before other accelerators, and likely would help with the
inter-program organisation problem because the information could be routed
to the proper program to allow them to connect. If we don't partner with
existing sites, we should crawl them for potential candidates to populate
our own with
-Partnerships with hack-a-day, hackster.io, and other hardware projects
sites to identify potential admits - maybe even guarantee a spot in a
program as an award to a contest that we judge. Maybe even
kickstarter/indiegogo

Also, if the documentary idea is still being entertained, I have someone we
should talk to. He created deadliest catch and storage wars, and I think he
would like this - he's a bit disheartened at the direction that he spurred
television.

No problem at all as to Monday - I appreciate the update.

Best,

Matthew

to: Andy Shannon <andy@startupbootcamp.org>
subject: Re: SBC Data from Alex
msg_id: 14f76ee80660d581
---

Hi Andy,

Thank you for the feedback. I really need to have my assumption about the
selection day field in the dataset confirmed and a few peripheral
datapoints (i.e. a measure of success) before I can draw any data-based
conclusions. Until then, it would be invalid to suggest anything more than
a trend as to a particular channel or activity being more effective than
another outside of what I have already outlined. However, based on
intuition, best practices, and in speaking to the rest of the team, some
suggestions I have are:

-Create a marketing campaign plan for the 3 month period with a
content/channel calendar
-Curate workshops, information sessions, guest lectures, advisor/SBC-staff
meet-and-greets, networking events, and other SBC-hosted events outside of
FastTrack, which really seems to just be a pitch feedback session from what
I can tell
-Provide resources to startups we'll eventually want to target (support,
advice, workspace, targeted events or workshops, etc). We could actually
get a pretty good snapshot of what this looks like in terms of
characteristics with the data it sounds like is already available.
-Getting outside partners into these events could help establish or
maintain those relationships, as well as piggy-back on the visibility of
larger organisations
-Generate content templates to allow programs to easily iterate quality web
productions, graphics, video (promotional, interviews, news, etc),
newsletters, podcasts, and other content, and distribute as necessary
-Plan touchpoints to reach out to alumni, advisors, investors, and partners
to encourage them to refer programs (this is about the only one that I can
really say is supported validly by the data thus far). I envision this
probably being 2 or 3 newsletters. There are a lot of ways we could
conceivably incentivise these referrals, but I need to know more about how
they generally occur and who is making them.
-Backlog interesting content throughout the year that is not time sensitive
and release it during the recruitment cycle to raise SEO performance,
visibility on social graph, and generally on digital. Additionally, recycle
past content that has done spectacularly during the recruitment cycle
-I don't exactly know how the applicants that are "contacted by SBC" are
reached out to, but I think the way this is done could have a HUGE impact
on if they eventually convert or not (let alone are receptive to the
outreach).
-An infographic at the end of each selection cycle to provide insight as to
what trends are in the startup ecosystem without giving away too much data
-Provide resources and insight into digital marketing infrastructure best
practices when not in recruitment cycles and less focus required on
campaign execution
-Allow people to register interest in particular programs outside of the
application cycle - then contact them when the cycle opens

I mean if we want to get really "creative", we could pitch a legitimate
documentary/reality TV show to PBS, TED, Motherboard, Engadget, G4, or
someone of the like. The idea is basically a dragon's den type pitch off
show, but also showing the subsequent progression through incubation and
valuable insight into launching and growing a business. This was definitely
a joke when I first thought of it, but given the interest in tech and
startups right now, as well as the lack of understanding of incubators and
really growing small businesses, this actually could be something. I also
know some pretty significant reality TV producers if we wanted to try.
Completely spitballing here, and frankly I'm sure it would be prohibitively
risky from both a legal and a brand standpoint.  It would certainly be
highly visible and brand-creating - although I don't think it's the brand
association SBC wants.

One of my takeaways with Marc was that there were over 600 applicants to
London FinTech last cycle, which brings to light just how massive the
complete data set is, and just how powerful the insight derived from the
full dataset could be. It was also very exciting to hear that he not only
was open to the idea of using machine learning to develop predictive
analytics, but had already put serious thought into it (and maybe had
already started?). It also somewhat confirmed that I should overcompensate
in terms of being clean cut, well-spoken, and letting the data do the
talking when necessary to counteract the perceptions around my age -
something very similar to healthcare actually.

Please let me know if there's anything else I can send along in terms of
elaboration on the what we've previously discussed, or additionally
production portfolios, references, or writing samples. Enjoy your time back
stateside.

Best,

Matthew

date: 2015-08-27
to: Andy Shannon <andy@startupbootcamp.org>
subject: Re: SBC Data from Alex
msg_id: 14f71759a1cb12b4
---

Hi Andy,

Assuming this data is the full data available to me and with limited time
to really evaluate it, I would say what could be immediately beneficial is
a series of 4 bespoke reports delivered to programs through the recruiting
process. One report would focus on the initial targeting of startups to
guide recruiting, one would provide input later into the recruitment
process to drive applications, one would aim to aid in the selection of
applicants to offer spots to, and one would be delivered after the
selection process as a high-level recap. These reports would highlight high
performers, identify deviations from typical recruiting patterns, outline
best practices, and eventually move towards predictive analytics.

5 examples of items I could see in the reports:
-Geographic breakdown of acceptances (there seems to be an extremely heavy
bias towards targeting and accepting local startups, but where else are
hotbeds?)
-Channel targeting breakdown (which channels have highest proportional
acceptance rate, lowest proportional acceptance rate, lead to our
objectively ideal applicant?)
-Trends in teams (it seems that in general, programs like teams with small
number cofounders, lots of employees, but not too many engineers)
-Suggesting that some startups may be better fits in an alternative program
(would need available info on status of recruiting at each program)
-Outline previously missed opportunities and general trends in decision
making (would need subsequent information on startup success)

These items could be phrased as series of insights (and maybe supporting
visuals) - something like, "your program's favourite recruiting channels
are X, the top performing program's favourite recruiting channel is Y, you
stand to improve your performance by Z by making ______ change." It should
be noted that some of these biases make complete sense (i.e. it's probably
much easier to recruit a local startup than one across international
borders, not to mention some locations are likely ripe for a certain type
of startup).

Again, this is based on the data I was given and the assumptions I stated,
as well as the assumption that program A is Amsterdam, B is Barcelona, and
C is Berlin (to be able to draw deeper geo conclusions).

If the selection day field is in fact the indication as to whether the
program accepted an invitation or was invited to the program, I could
actually go ahead and generate the report. However from my conversation
with Marc today, it sounds like this is a very small swatch of data, and
more data equals more accuracy.

Best,

Matthew

date: 2015-08-27
to: Andy Shannon <andy@startupbootcamp.org>
subject: Re: SBC Data from Alex
msg_id: 14f6ca1d6d24312f
---

Hi Andy,

Please find below a list of ideas regarding insight that could be gained
through analysis of the data at our disposal (although there would likely
be some necessary tweaks in terms of survey design to provide more useful
data):

   - Optimise candidate targeting by unearthing factors that correlate to
   post-SBC success
   - Optimise recruitment path (order and frequency of touch points) to
   increase conversions (i.e. accepted offers)
   - Provide data to aid in selection process to reduce false positives and
   negatives
   - Evaluate individual program performance and push feedback to create
   informational social conformity
   - Benchmark overall SBC performance
   - Generally optimise the recruitment funnel (there are likely elements
   outside of the scope of the dataset I was provided)


First steps:

   - Complete collection and cleaning of the data Alex was working on
   - Redesign survey/application forms for better data collection, to
   provide a few more factors we can analyse, and generally complete the scope
   of the data (i.e. post-incubation data)
   - Identify biases in selection process and make programs aware so can
   compensate if undesirable
   - Identify desirable factors of recruits that indicate future success


A more out-there idea:

   - Compare ourselves to other accelerators/incubators - by adding the
   question "Have you applied to other accelerators/incubators" we could gain
   data on other programs' rejections. Scraping public data will give us the
   data on their acceptances. Subsequently using machine learning could give
   us truly unique predictive analytics on the startup ecosystem.


I tried to keep them pretty high level, but let me know if you want me to
elaborate on anything.

I also wanted to mention that I received a formal offer from another
company today and will need to respond to them relatively soon.

Best,

Matthew

to: Tucker Gumber <tuckerthefestivalguy@gmail.com>
subject: FestEvo App ASO
msg_id: 14f4265bbc143a20
---

Hi Tucker,

I wanted to reach out, as I know we had been in touch a year or so ago
about festevo but I dropped off a bit. Sorry I never followed up, I was
quite swamped searching for a full time job and moving to London. Anyways,
I've been doing a lot of app marketing recently, and was wondering if you
might be interested in letting me help you out a bit if you're still
actively working on festevo.

A lot of my recent work has been in App Store Optimization (ASO), or making
apps more searchable and visible in store fronts. This directly results
from obvious factors such as downloads and ratings, but also from less
visible ones such as your store description, your photos, download rate per
visitor, keywords, etc. Basically, I want to overhaul your ASO for free
(which usually charge upwards for $500 as a freelancer)

Recently, I overhauled the ASO at a company I had been working for, Touch
Surgery, and we saw our downloads jump from where it had been slowing
climbing to at about 600 per day to 1,500 overnight. After a week, we were
fluctuating between 4,000 and 5,500 downloads per day. We also hit #1
medical app and top #500 overall app in over 30 different countries.

Really, I just think what you're working on is much better than the
fragmented festival-specific app organisers seem to insist on having built
via outsourcing. I'm also trying to move back towards music tech in my
career a bit more, and thought this would be a good step.

Let me know if that might be of interest and we can hop on a call.

Best,

Matthew

Hi Laura,

So I've broken down my time below. Looking at that breakdown, I'm
definitely going to have to stick firm at $750 per month, and I am actually
going to be raising the price of this significantly for future clients.

In terms of time:
Twitter Posts - 10 hours per month - 2,000 outreach tweets per month, 100
content tweets/retweets per month
Facebook Posts: 8 hours per month - 15 posts per month (the life of a
facebook post is 2 days, so no point squashing it's reach with another)
Facebook Ads: 2 hours per month - $50 per month
Instagram Posts: 10 hours per month - Growth hacking instagram is still a
very manual process, but I think this would be fun
Analytics: 3 hours per month

My other costs are overhead and allow me to execute the scripts needed to
tweet 100 times per hour and follow as many users as I want, so I can't
really itemise them. Also, please keep in mind, this does not include a
image template kit, so the content I use will not be branded/under a
consistent template.

Best,

Matthew

I assume by clip you're referring to a video clip? I offer two options for
that, depending on what you're looking for. I partner with someone for
video production, and between us we generally can supply all necessary
professional equipment, produce all scripts and shotlists, provide any
necessary actors and locations (within reason), edit the video, and release
the video. Price can fluctuate depending on the complexity of the video.

-Promo Video: video has become the keystone of digital content marketing.
It is the most viral, the most highly engaged with, the lowest cost per
impression to distribute, and the most concise type of media. It is a
minimum barrier to entry for most app companies, as well as for
crowdfunding raises and press campaigns. A clear and well produced video
can compound all of your inbound and viral marketing efforts. My partner
and I will work with you to create a script and shot list to your liking
and then produce a video to your liking. Price can alter quite a bit
depending on your needs or input. You can see examples of this here
<http://t.sidekickopen17.com/e1t/c/5/f18dQhb0S7lC8dDMPbW2n0x6l2B9nMJN7t5XZsQsBhjW1qMyFK5wvHZnVRJgRK56dP4Wf34C7ZF02?t=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.youtube.com%2Fwatch%3Fv%3DmFESQmdjE98&si=5804247449337856&pi=83bad29b-b65d-469c-9636-28615983ec17>
and here
<http://t.sidekickopen17.com/e1t/c/5/f18dQhb0S7lC8dDMPbW2n0x6l2B9nMJN7t5XZsQsBhjW1qMyFK5wvHZnVRJgRK56dP4Wf34C7ZF02?t=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.youtube.com%2Fwatch%3Fv%3Dsb1wfD6Anww&si=5804247449337856&pi=83bad29b-b65d-469c-9636-28615983ec17>
.

-Video Series Template: great for if you have an idea for set of videos.
We'll produce an easy-to-iterate template for the series, documentation on
how to produce future episodes, as well as produce the first episode.
Examples of this can be seen here
<http://t.sidekickopen17.com/e1t/c/5/f18dQhb0S7lC8dDMPbW2n0x6l2B9nMJN7t5XZsQsBhjW1qMyFK5wvHZnVRJgRK56dP4Wf34C7ZF02?t=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.youtube.com%2Fplaylist%3Flist%3DPLjcyqLPt8BG45Hrf2myu0cHBlOHovNjqT&si=5804247449337856&pi=83bad29b-b65d-469c-9636-28615983ec17>

Okay, this is a RIDICULOUSLY long presentation. I've included a bunch of
comments, some of which can be applied across the rest of the presentation,
but am still really only halfway into the general FAQ. Given how long this
document is, I would suggest trying to embed interlinking within the
document as much as makes sense.

I'm getting pretty nitpicky on a lot of these. However, the big one to me
is the links/calls to action - they're there, they're not there, they
change form, and frankly i find them a bit clunky.

I'll continue to edit this tomorrow and over the weekend, and hopefully can
get through all of it by Monday.

https://relayto.com/axa/UYYYEZ5L


*Top 10:*
-Love that this idea and how it's up front, but lack of any introduction is
sort of weird to me without at least an inline table of contents (i know
there's one to the side, but it's sort of peripheral to me - maybe refer to
alex on this one)
-Maybe streamline the answers into two sentences or so each, remove any
graphics, and don't have them as dropdowns
-1. contact us link leads to a contact us page - any ways we can make it
lead somewhere more direct i.e. an email support link, provide a popup with
call-line? might not be one
-1. delete "Of course" in second bullet, use active voice (makes, not has
made), delete yourself
-2. The word "excess" is weird for me, but I think it's because we use the
term premium or deductible instead?
-2. You go from talking to the client to at them - I would remove the
second line, make a stronger call to action in the second sentence of the
first line, and hyperlink the verb or subject
-3. uncapitalize "mobile"
-3. "...would like to cover it away..."
-3. Link personal possessions, not a separate sentence
-4. Weird spacing on first bullet
-4. I like the GIF except the camera moves making a pretty jarring jump in
frame - can you find a similar one where the umbrella stays still in the
frame? Regardless, now I think I take back the streamline answers comment
-4. Change last line to "Receive a contents insurance quote" - streamline
communication of benefit
-5. Put this slide last in the top 10 maybe? It's what AXA wants people not
to do, so it looks bad that high up the FAQ (i.e. 'that many people want to
cancel???')
-6. Weird that this slide has a background and none of the others do. Maybe
do go ahead with streamlining the slides and getting good quality slide
backgrounds instead? Or maybe too much visual stimulation that way.
-6. Replace "like" with "such as"
-6. Second sentence, delete up to "Cost of repairing" and start sentence
there
-6. Change last line to "Receive a contents insurance quote" - streamline
communication of benefit
-7. Awkward place to suggest receiving a quote
-8. "coverage" not "cover"
-8. "...first arrange a quote or by logging..."
-9. in title say "significantly", not "a lot"
-10. "...print them whenever you would like."
-10. "View my documents..." - for all instances of this


*General FAQ*

What do I do if my property is uninhabitable?
-Delete second part of the sentence
-Change "property" to "home"

How will I be kept informed...
-"...status of your claim instantly anytime in your AXA Account."
-Link in first sentence your AXA Account mention, not at end

What happens after I've told you about...
-Change title to "What happens after I've submitted my claim?"
-"When you file a claim, we'll call you to discuss what action is needed."
-Second bullet seems like a different FAQ point

Who will deal with my claim?
-"...managing your claim as quickly as possible" - efficiently sounds to
impersonal
-Second bullet is a very long sentence, second half is kind of redundant in
context of 3rd bullet
-The call to action/link on this one is better format, although still a bit
long

If I'm making a building claim and a contents claim
-comma in title between claim and do
-Inconsistent CTA wording with one in the question above

What forms will I
-Delete second sentence of first bullet
-Again inconsistent CTA/link

What If I don't know the dates
-First bullet "...Account, you can find your previous claim details by
loggin in online."
-Put hyperlink in reference above, not below

I need to send you my...
-Title breaks form with every other title thus far - rephrase to fit
previous form
-Why is the map on a different slide? Also, I'm not really sure what the
map adds apart from show off content versatility on relayto, which is maybe
a good enough reason to include it

Do I need to wait...
-You break form from all your previous answers here
-"Yes, however..."

When will my claim be approved
-Delete "of course"
-"how long it takes" is too colloquial, use a more formal and concise
phrase - processing time maybe?

What information do i need to provide
-Call to action should be embedded at mention of AXA Account in second
bullet
-Log in, not use in second bullet
-Take out comma in second sentence of third bullet
-"If anything has been lost or stolen, inform the police..."

strategies - I didn't want to misquote any numbers here, but to provide
some more concrete examples. This is pretty long, so I also summarized in 3
attached slides:

*ASO*
-Touch Surgery has been my most hands on ASO project
     iOS Keyword: we currently rank in the top ten for 23 keywords,
compared to 5 in September 2014
     Country Rank: Quarterly high country ranking average for Top 10
Countries (Sept 2014 in parentheses): 6.4 (96.1), Top 25 Countries: 7.2
(88.0) (Top countries measured in terms of app downloads nationwide)
     Results: 80k downloads in July 2015, up from 13k in September 2014

2nd at TC Disrupt

this fall.

*SEO*

        -Implemented SEO across over 170 web pages and 200 pieces of media
        -Analysed results and re-optimised SEO targeting
        -See attached slides for sample metrics

you already are

-This is a particularly tricky rollout as it's not a latin-based language -

date: 2015-08-03
to: Vivian Chan <vc@sparrho.com>
subject: Re: Intro - Matthew, Vivian (Sparrho)
msg_id: 14ef3eaca4449d01
---

Digital Marketing is the entire focus of what I do, so I'm very curious
where you saw a CV that didn't mention that. I have a very unique
background in marketing that combines academic research, a corporate-style
marketing education, production know-how, heavy data analytics, and silicon
valley digital startup/private sector experience that I have very
specifically developed over the past 5 years.

I have planned and implemented SEO for at least 10 different companies
(including a Hachette Filipacchi publications with an Alexa rank in the top
2500 globally) and PPC for over 5 in my career as an independent marketing
consultant. Generally, I find that returns are much much higher for
companies that are willing to take a holistic approach to digital marketing
(frankly isolating SEO from your other efforts is really not a good idea,
as SEO is dependent on your other efforts). However, I'm not sure if what
you're looking for is a search and search ad expert or a digital marketing
expert - based on your comments above, it seems like you're after the
former, as I am the latter.

I should mention that you should be aware that asking for examples of SEO
and PPC doesn't really make very much sense. SEO is based on inputs that
are for the most part obscured upon viewing a website unless you open the
element inspector in Chrome and know what you're looking for. The site
architecture/infrastructure side of SEO also has very different
implementation techniques depending on specific organisational goals. What
you should be asking for is client lists, content examples (as this is
where tangible output from SEO can be seen), website traffic history, or
for a brief SEO evaluation of your existing efforts. If you're asking for
analytics of SEO/PPC performance, that information is subject to NDA's with
my prior clients, and I can not share it.  This is for pretty much true for
all SEO professionals - which means if they're willing to show YOU
something, they're also willing to show other people YOUR data. I would be
more than happy to discuss how I have managed these campaigns and
high-level results from them and can provide a few quantitative metrics in
person, but must respect the agreements I have made with my past clients.

As per PPC, this is only visible while campaigns are active. Bottom line:
if you're serious about PPC, you should be outsource it, although I have
certainly set up campaigns for clients who did not wish to do so - really
only useful if you have a spend under £300 or so. Unless you have 3 or 4
people to devote full time to PPC, you will see higher ROI from an
outsourced campaign. Video is certainly the highest ROI PPC channel, which
is usually not covered via PPC outsourcing, and is something I have a great
deal of experience with.

If you'd like examples of content production, press relations, web design,
keyword planning analysis, site architecture mapping, campaign execution,
or userbase growth, I would be happy to include information or portfolios
along those lines - SEO truly is pretty useless on it's own, but as an
amalgamation of all of the aforementioned channels, becomes far and away
the most powerful tool in digital marketing.

Please find attached a copy of my CV, as I don't seem to have sent it to
you at any point in the past.

to: Alex Shevelenko <alex@glocalpartners.com>
subject: Re: Ollie May shared with you "Proposal to Change All Proposals"
msg_id: 14edc0d82ad3c885
---

Sorry for the delay on this - find feedback below!


Background:
-I wouldn’t refer to specific companies - something like “…digital
experience on their computers and mobiles devices.” ?
-“short-term” instead of “near-term” before the list
-First sentence in last paragraph is a bit hard to digest - split into two
sentences

Two Problems…:
-1st Break first sentence into two. “The first goal of a proposal…”
-1st Last sentence: “…delivering 10’s and 100’s of pages of traditional
documents…”
-2nd First P “…require a significant amount of organisational effort”
-Great annotations - gives me some ideas for some of my presentations.
Can’t decide if i like the consistency of the calls to action “Find out…”
or not, but it would be hard to come up with 16 different ones so stick
with that.

Wow Factor:
-Nice citation :) In general I like this slide a lot though.
-Add a line break at the top of the left column of text to align it with
the bottom of the right and create even spacing between the bottom of the
slide and the top of the ribbon button
-Immerse: take our comma between beautiful and visual
-Simplify interactivity sounds a bit clunky - try using 3 something with 3
words to be consistent with the first bullets structure
-Use periods at end of second sentence on both bullets

Personalised:
-Hyper: has a lot of dashes and adjectives - simply
-Package: title is clunky - try to fit it in the first line
-Use periods at end of second sentence on both bullets

Video:
-Don’t mention rich media here - you talk about it in the next section
-Like the usage of deluge, but use overloaded instead. Split into two
sentences
-The slide underneath doesn’t really add anything

Any Media:
-First sentence is confusing with all the everywhere one place - make
simpler
-Second sentence is awkward
-I’m pretty sure this is the first time you’ve referred to Relayto by name
apart from in the video slide above - I’m generally of the belief do so as
often as makes sense but not to excess. The more times you can get someone
to process the word, the more likely they will be to remember it

Interactive Workshops:
-2 and’s in a sentence is sometimes okay - 3 and’s is too much and should
be truncated or split into multiple sentences

Real-Time Collaboration:
-Say “evangelists” instead of “customer champion” - this sentence is
generally a bit clunky
-Last sentence “Ensure” not “ing”

Shareable:
-Left column text spacing
-“directly from Relayto”

Tracking:
-Second sentence is very awkward - questions change structure
-Split into two points - Measure and Discover/Improve/Something
aspirational about using data

Timely Delivery:
-First sentence seems redundant
-I would maybe split this into two points - one about speed, and one about
chronology. The fact that I can update an already distributed document is a
huge benefit of Relayto to me, as I’m never stuck banging my head against
the wall over a typo that already went out on some document or realising I
could have included something that would have been very compelling.

AutoTag:
-AutoTag sounds like a branded term - is it? If not, split the words and
use automatically
-Use & instead of and in title (that’s what you use across all the others)
-Search across: lots of dashes again
-Search beyond: awkward to use “search” in both of the subheadings (and the
main one)
-Search beyond: “search” used 3 times in first 3 lines
-Search beyond: last sentence is very awkward

Centralised:
-Doesn’t really communicate benefit - when i think centralised I often
think bureaucratic approval processes and clearances

Reusable:
-change “tuning” to “fine-tuning”
-I would change this into “Iterate and customise” and “Work smarter” - make
iterate about cloning and fine tuning and work smarter about resourcing
existing slides or blocks of presentation and repurposing them

Footnotes:
-A bit odd how format changes

Hi Nikita,

Hope you're having a good weekend.

I've finally compiled my notes for July, but haven't had time to put them

date: 2015-07-19
to: Mathieu Garcia <mathieu.garcia@intua.net>
subject: Re: Reaching out
msg_id: 14ea744b87f61e9e
---

Hi Mathieu,

I've actually been using Twitter App Ads for the Touch Surgery app -
they're pretty effective, and I imagine would be even more so for a
music/entertainment app as compared with a medical app. Additionally,
Google AdWords has recently unveiled direct-to-download ads for mobile
search users, which have proven very effective for me. Also, just ASO/SEO
in general and trying to make contact with Apple App Store curators and
other influencers will be huge.

As per teaser, I actually have made quite a few of these (mostly for
app-based products, which are very difficult to film), and am actually
currently working on one right now for TS. I think their are a few ways we
could approach it for BM3, and maybe do it as part of a series. In general,
video is the highest ROI form of digital content, so I definitely think
this is an avenue we should pursue. We should discuss video in general, but
I have most of the equipment that would be necessary to film professional
quality promo videos already, so it wouldn't even be particularly costly to
get started. I can usually crank out a video in 3 days or so once the
script and shots are sorted (which can range in time depending on if we're
looking to film in venues, studios, etc.).

There are a few things on the actual product side we should discuss as well
in terms of viral looping, onboarding, and engagement optimization that
will likely be huge in bolstering growth rates. As per launch date, we
should shoot for mid-November to give us time to establish presence on the
app store and optimize marketing a bit in time for the holiday season. As
with retail, app consumption and especially purchase is at annual high
points in December (and January as well, unlike retail).

Anyways, we can discuss all of this soon! Looking forward to it.

Matthew

Head of Marketing, the Head of Sales, and the COO at Touch Surgery and have
soft buy-in from all of them  - the COO asked how it was different than
say, slideshare, and when I described it he was very impressed. Now I just
need to show them a few branded examples of what it can do, which is the
main purpose of this email.

I'm making a few pieces of content to show them, and on this one, it
appears that #8 and #9 in my listicle have disappeared from the live view:
https://relayto.com/matteisn/ULy0ZVyO

However, they still show up in the editor mode. Any suggestions? I've also
included a document that I'm including UI/UX issues and notes, as well as
bug lists here:
https://docs.google.com/document/d/1qbXKdFeHBTQCXIU7CY50bmxoL4-si1gJcQub-rMPotw/edit?usp=sharing


I'll go back and collate my previous notes into this as well, although let
me know if you have a better system for this - usually I would use a
spreadsheet, but need a better understanding of Nikita's workflow and the
platform in general to be able to make one that would really be useful.

Also, I was wondering if I should/can get access to a Replyto slack account.

Talk to you tomorrow,

Matthew

date: 2015-06-23
to: Alex Shevelenko <alex@glocalpartners.com>
subject: Re: Relayto Best Practices Tutorial V1
msg_id: 14e2282c395b7c45
---

I just looked over what I sent you and realised I didn't really organise
high and low level feedback very well. I've restructured it below. Sorry
for the mass that was!

Feedback/edits:

General:
-Scrolling is kind of rough
-Need file/page loading indicator on launch
-Looks a bit odd when you pop out the right menu and it cuts off the text
-Formalised names for UI elements might be a good idea. I could do this if
you'd like - would probably help me get an in-depth knowledge of the UI
-I certainly get using branded content for the examples, but we could
probably go farther and inspire some creativity if we used some of our own,
at least until some outside evangelists started creating truly fascinating
content - although I also imagine it's easier to bridge the product gap for
users this way
-It might be cool to have some sort of preview function where you can see
how the file will look on different screens and devices - a big concern for
me in digital content creation and distribution
-Need some sort of audio loading/playing (and preferably scrolling)
indicator (specifically in the Rocket Fuel presentation)
-Can we have a way to remove page numbers/crop pages down on imported decks
to avoid the page numbering issue?
-Hyperlinking within the doc seems a bit complicated - but it's extremely
good SEO practice to have different URLs for each slide

Importing PDF Slides

   1. Make images higher contrast
   2. "You can allow readers to view or download the original document if
   you would like... (how? by placing a link? Clarify and instruct)”

Background

   1. Subheadings are the same size as headings
   2. Cut-off text in top screenshot looks bad, but realise thats a UI thing
   3. I don’t see the tile button - would be cool if it was a gif of 3
   shots with a highlighted mouse showing an upload (or is the tile button
   thing only relevant as a quick fix for this particular bug?)
   4. In slide background, say “left-hand tool bar” - left hand bar is vague

Cover Photo

   1. This section is confusing. I’ve come up with 3 different
   possibilities for what using a blank png could mean - and the second image
   actually confuses me more. Is the background the city and the upload was a
   png logo with a transparent background? Are you saying that if you set the
   slide background of a presentation as a logo, to upload a blank png so it
   shows through (and if so, can’t there just be a transparent setting?)
   2. high resolution - how high, and give ideal dimensions. I imagine this
   could get quite complicated in terms of screen sizes and cropping.

Example of Content

   1. Right hand bar made me look to the tutorial navigation bar. I think
   we might need to name this

Adding Content

   1. Heading/subheading sizing the same
   2. First sentence directs people to the next step, but I still don’t
   know what you mean by “interactive content”.
   3. Images: what do you mean by the description area - is there another
   way to upload?
   4. Images: Using the same image three times on this is confusing. Also,
   I don’t get what happened? I think this would look better as a 3 shot gif
   with highlighted mouse where you can see the process you’re talking through
   5. Creating images: call it “Image Sizing Guide” - don’t be platform
   specific - also, will there be the ability to crop images?
   6. Video: UI elements from screenshot are confusing (particularly top
   left three dots and the two sets of arrows and "Start writing”. Definitely
   crop in, but also those bounded arrows will still be there :/ Also, where
   is there a full chrome browser within the embedded screenshot with an
   embedded video?
   7. Video: first sentence is a bit of a mouthful. second sentence say
   “Then, click…” - instruct, don’t suggest

Annotations

   1. First sentence, put quotes around Annotate when you use it the second
   time in reference to the menu item.
   2. Second sentence: “Then select the image…”
   3. Second column: put “but it is less powerful” in parentheses
   4. Images are very small and not sized consistently - see image section
   of content  ;)
   5. “Don’t clutter the page with too many annotation boxes. Instead, aim
   to place a few highly relevant boxes that are easily visible and clickable
   from a mobile device.”
   6. Column text layout is odd.

Editing

   1. "Relayto has many editing tools”
   2. First paragraph in general is a bit confusing
   3. In terms of annotations, is there a cursor indicator to show that
   you’re on annotation mode and not type mode
   4. Nice touch giving an example on that requires a small subsequent
   interaction to expose them to more features/UI function
   5. “pop up bar, you can find” in last paragraph

Dividers

   1. Still think we should call it the left sidebar or something like that
   2. Think a gif showing three dots> settings>add divider could be cool
   3. Change 'Make sure the text color… …left hand bar, “settings.”' to
   “You can edit the color of text in the divider under the left-hand
   toolbar>settings.  (be consistent with how you reference structure elements
   of UI - aka x>y>z vs. x, “y”
   4. ‘…the text color in both “post view” and “presentation view" is the
   same, select, deselect, and reselect the color you want.”

Table of Contents

   1. Table of ContentS*
   2. Take out “(in Powerpoint, Word, or Canva)” and explain why you would
   want to add images and icons
   3. Hyperlinking protocol - does it have to be another slide, or can it
   be ANY slide in step 1?

Company Name

   1. “…be sure to deselect your name if you do not wish for it to appear.”

Top Bar

   1. Headers/Subheaders same size
   2. “…want to make it public or share it with someone.”
   3. Put feature button terms in quotations
   4. Wait, widget bar? theres another bar? Don’t refer to a bar within a
   bar, call the embedded one a menu or something.

date: 2015-06-17
to: aliciaburke@gwmail.gwu.edu
subject: Copy for submissions
msg_id: 14e00ce7a9d500b0
---

Touch Surgery was founded by surgeons with a vision of raising the
standards of global surgery through the use of mobile technology. By
combining core concepts from gaming, surgical training, and cognitive task
analysis, we've created highly engaging and accurate training and rehearsal
simulations for surgical experts, medical students, and enthusiasts alike.
Touch Surgery has already been integrated into surgical training
curriculums and is used by hundreds of thousands of surgical trainees and
leading surgeons in every country on earth, who strive to improve their
technical skills and surgical decision making. Additionally, we are
constantly establishes partnerships with leading healthcare institutions
and associations in order to develop the most cutting edge and accurate
interactive learning modules available anywhere, anytime.

Touch Surgery is designed for hardware that sits in most people's pockets
already (ie: smart devices like an iPhone), which makes it easily adoptable
and potentially infinitely scalable. By offering our simulator on mobile
platforms, we allow surgeons and surgical trainees to improve their skills
at any time - be it between operations, on their commute to work, or whilst
at home - anywhere in the world. To create our simulations, we partner with
leading surgeons, institutions, and organisations such as Stanford, Duke,
and UCL, and many others, and employ animators who have worked on Finding
Nemo, Avatar, Gravity, Harry Potter, and 007 movies.

date: 2015-06-16
to: Alex Shevelenko <alex@glocalpartners.com>
subject: Replyto Platform Notes
msg_id: 14dfbf3c27ea06d0
---

Note: From producing 2 articles for entertainment/knowledge dissemination.
I still want to do one more exercise using Replyto for a slide deck or
pitch to see how it feels in a more professional use case before I'd be
comfortable saying this is a comprehensive but surface level overview.

-Editor Features: All in all, the editor was much more robust than I first
realised. However, I wasn't actually aware of a lot of the features until I
accidentally performed a few actions that showed them to me (i.e.
highlighting a text snippet pulls up rich text editor, column creation,
outline tool)
-Solution: Tutorials videos, A/B test UX, focus groups

-Clarity of Icons/Indicators: I must say, I love some of the UI elements
you use. The little arrow on the right hand side to indicate which section
you're editing is a beautiful touch. However, I'm not sure which content
block it's pointing to! In generally, the UI is very elegant, but needs to
be a bit clearer/"idiotproofed". This also could help resolve the issue
with not understanding some of the scope and function of the various
features on the platform.
-Solution: Interactive onboarding tutorial, focus groups

-Portfolios: I think this will be a major driver for early adoption - to
encourage evangelism, we need to make users portfolios something they're
proud that they can showcase. We spoke a lot about building the foundations
for and the dissemination of individual pieces of content, but the true way
to drive platform adoption is to get people to share the platform, not
individual pieces of content.

-Distribution Strategy: I'm very curious to hear how the content will be
made available. Obviously I've seen the current iteration of the web
platform. Will there be an app? Export function? Also, how will these be
shareable/embeddable? What about in terms of content development and
collaboration tools? Can multiple people work on the same piece of content
at once (as a side, a friend of mine who was really the
hardware/software/firmware brains behind the gTar, created a web-based
collaboration-enabled DAW (audio production software suite) that sees about
2ms of latency - just to say that if we wanted to implement a super-fast
web-based collaboration feature, he could probably help)?

-Content Formatting Issues: Some content types have text that bleeds out of
the content embed, particularly when the content is changed to a
non-standard display format. Also, there should be a way to batch edit like
pieces of content or set default formatting (i.e. I had to go through each
content block I made individually and switch them to a different display
format - I actually only did this as a workaround to the bleeding content I
mentioned above).

annual meeting, so when you guys are looking at booking for your agenda,
let's chat - if they can get a speaking slot, I think we could pretty much
guarantee that we'll be there, and can bring along Oculus/zSpace and pull
out all the stops. If not, we'll have to play it by ear, although I think
we'd at least want to table.

We'd also really love to explore a more formal partnership with ASiT. I
mentioned the community element that we're rolling out at a few
universities in the US and with the RCSEd. I think you guys would be a
great candidate to have early access. It could prove really valuable in
terms of having a channel to consolidate relevant information, facilitate
interesting discussion, and general create an avenue for your members to
connect through, as well as position ASiT as a thought leader to our
userbase of now over 250k people. What would be the logical progression for
making this happen or who would we have to get in front of?

Best,

Matthew

In terms of about me, I work on the edge of behavioural science, digital

for startups. I've worked with quite a few companies building out product
portfolios, digital platforms, and designing viral looping mechanisms.

Some notable successes: I helped design the Incident gTar
<http://t.sigopn03.com/e1t/c/5/f18dQhb0S7lC8dDMPbW2n0x6l2B9nMJN7t5XZsQsBhjW1qMyFK5wvHZnVRJgRK56dP4Wf34C7ZF02?t=http%3A%2F%2Fincidentgtar.com%2F&si=5804247449337856&pi=2703ba34-6314-47f9-ceb4-b8283cf5bec6>
